#### Architect ask #1 verdict — F-72 is a coherent F-24 variant, not a weakening

F-24 in this file (export pipeline) reads "audit-BEFORE-side-effect": the export audit row commits before the Blob URL is created and the file leaves the worker's browser. F-58 (retention sweep) generalises this to "audit-WITH-side-effect": the `retention.deleted` summary row is the LAST write inside a transaction whose deletes have already executed. F-72 (backup) is a THIRD shape — *manifest-WRITTEN-pending-before-upload, status-finalized-after, audit-emitted-after-finalize* — and we need to verify it preserves the same invariant.

- **The shared invariant (F-24, F-58, F-72):** *no claim of a side-effect having occurred commits without its audit/manifest anchor, and the anchor's content cannot overstate what actually happened.*
- **F-24 (export):** audit emitted first; if the audit fails, the side-effect (Blob URL creation) is never reached. The audit row is the claim; the side-effect follows the claim.
- **F-58 (retention sweep):** deletes accumulate inside a tx; summary row is written LAST inside the same tx; if the summary throws, the entire tx rolls back including the deletes. Single atomicity unit.
- **F-72 (backup):** the manifest row is written in `pending` status BEFORE the upload (the manifest is the audit anchor for the upload), then the upload happens, then the manifest transitions to `committed` (on success) or `aborted_<reason>` (on failure). The audit row (`backup.manifest_written`) is emitted AFTER the transition to committed. The state machine is `(no manifest) → pending → (committed | aborted_<reason>) → audit emitted`. Key claim: a manifest in `committed` status is a verifiable claim that the upload received a success ACK (G-T11-29 lesson); a manifest in `aborted_*` status is a verifiable claim that the upload failed with a specific structured reason; a manifest in `pending` status is a verifiable claim that the upload was attempted but the status finalisation crashed (this is the legitimate "stale pending" state that T18's reconciliation surfaces).

The invariant holds: the manifest's status field is the claim surface; the status transition is the moment-of-truth; the audit row is supplementary (its emit failure does NOT roll back the upload, because the manifest itself is the persistent record). Two cases need pinning:

1. **Manifest write fails before upload attempt** (step 7 fails): NO upload attempted; no `__debugListPutCalls` entry; return `{status: 'errored', error_code: 'manifest_write_failed'}`. **Invariant preserved**: no upload claim without manifest.
2. **Upload succeeds but `transitionManifestStatus(committed)` fails** (step 9 throws after step 8 ACKs): manifest stays in `pending`; T17.1's single-tx wrapper makes this case structurally impossible at the SQL boundary (the tx rolls back both the upload — via revoking the put — and the pending manifest); the library captures it via the next-pass reconciliation (a pending manifest older than the lease window is surfaced as a stale state). **Invariant preserved**: a pending manifest is a known recoverable state, not a false-committed claim.

**Verdict:** F-72 is a coherent F-24 variant (third shape; state-machine variant), not a weakening. Test obligations T17-INVERSION-1 (pending-before-upload order observable), T17-INVERSION-2 (each rejection-reason → aborted status), T17-INVERSION-3 (manifest-write failure → no upload) pin the invariant directly.

#### Architect ask #2 verdict — F-71 is a NEW SURFACE

Walked §3.1–§3.9 for an object-lock-as-store-side-invariant equivalent. None of T05 (auth+session), T07 (E2EE keys), T08 (concern intake), T10 (inspection sync), T11 (export), T12 (export retention), T13 (reprisal), T14 (work refusal), or T16 (retention sweep) ship a storage primitive whose write-once-then-immutable contract is enforced at the store boundary. The closest precedent is the F-58 single-transaction atomicity invariant, but that is a transaction-scoped guarantee (within one tx, ordering + rollback) — not a multi-pass immutability contract at the storage layer. F-71 is structurally different:

- **F-58:** "within one transaction, no write commits unless ALL writes succeed." Time-scope: single tx.
- **F-71:** "across the 42-day lock window, no actor — including the writing role itself — can overwrite or delete this object." Time-scope: 42 days, across many txs, across many processes, across many code-paths.

The cooperative-caller defense is also a new pattern: the library exposes `putWithObjectLock(object_ref, blob, lock_until_ms)` for testability (the test can vary `lock_until_ms` via `__debugForceUnlockedAtMs`) but the production caller (`runBackupPass`) computes `lock_until_ms` from `BACKUP_OBJECT_LOCK_DAYS` exclusively. The library NEVER exposes a `lock_duration_ms` config field. This is the same shape as F-84 (no caller-supplied predicate), but applied to a time-bounded immutability contract rather than a query predicate.

**Verdict:** F-71 is a NEW SURFACE. Test obligations T17-OBJECT-LOCK-1/2/3 establish the library-side invariant; T17.1-BUCKET-POLICY-1 ratifies at the S3-compatible boundary.

#### Architect ask #3 verdict — F-83 is LOAD-BEARING; scored accordingly

The three fields (`audit_log_head`, `per_event_row_counts`, `retention_sweep_runs_snapshot_ts_ms`) are not "nice-to-have manifest metadata" — they are the literal join surface T18's reconciliation uses to attribute a divergence. RA-2 trigger #3 reads: *"any divergence between the live chain and the most recent pg_dump backup for a row older than the dump fires on FIRST occurrence regardless of cause."* The compensating control is "the pg_dump backup is the secondary witness" — but a witness with no testimony format is no witness at all. The three fields are the testimony format:

- `audit_log_head: {id, ts_ms, hash}` — defines "the most recent pg_dump backup" as a specific chain position. Without it, the divergence check has no stable anchor (which audit_log row do we compare against the live chain?).
- `per_event_row_counts` — defines what was IN the dump per event type. Without it, a row absent from the live chain cannot be attributed to (a) a legitimate sweep delete (which would show in the next pass's counts) vs (b) an unattributed tamper.
- `retention_sweep_runs_snapshot_ts_ms` — defines WHEN the dump observed the sweep checkpoint. Without it, sweep deletes that happened post-dump cannot be distinguished from tamper deletes; both look like "row gone from live chain, present in last dump."

If F-83 fails (any field missing, renamed, zeroed, or aggregated-to-sentinel on committed manifests), RA-2 trigger #3 fires on the next reconciliation pass because there is no stable comparison anchor. The score is **Low residual at the library boundary** (because the library structurally enforces it via the type system + the snapshot-pinned field names), but **the score is conditional on T17-RA2-ANCHOR-2** (the field-name snapshot pin) being a hard CI test — without it, a future innocuous rename ("let's call it `chain_head` for brevity") silently breaks the join. The test obligation is the structural seal.

**Verdict:** Scored Low residual; the load-bearing nature is reflected in the test obligation being a snapshot pin (rename-detection), not just an existence check.

#### Architect ask #4 verdict — RA-2 compensating control #4 is STRENGTHENED by T17

Pre-T17, RA-2 compensating control #4 was narrative: "the pg_dump backup is the secondary witness." The witness existed (ADR-0012 ratified the daily pg_dump) but the witness's testimony format was unstructured — a Postgres dump with no companion manifest carrying head-pointer, per-event counts, or sweep-snapshot timestamp. T18's reconciliation job would have to (a) load the entire dump into a staging Postgres, (b) compute its own head-pointer by scanning `audit_log` in the staging copy, (c) compute its own per-event histogram, (d) guess at the sweep state at dump-start, and (e) attempt to compare against the live chain — a fragile, expensive, error-prone path.

T17 strengthens the witness by giving it a structured manifest that exposes the join surface DIRECTLY:

- **Before T17:** witness = opaque pg_dump blob; reconciliation = full restore + scan.
- **After T17:** witness = pg_dump blob + structured manifest carrying `(audit_log_head, per_event_row_counts, retention_sweep_runs_snapshot_ts_ms, sha256, kid, schedule_hash, node_runtime_pin)`; reconciliation = jsonb comparison against the manifest row + live `audit_log` SELECT at `audit_log_head.id`.

The strengthening claim is verified by walking the T18 reconciliation algorithm:

1. T18 reads the most recent `backup_manifests` row with `status='committed'` (manifest-side; no blob fetch needed for the diff check).
2. T18 reads the live `audit_log` row at `audit_log_head.id`; compares `audit_log.hash` against `manifest.audit_log_head.hash`.
3. If hash matches: no tamper at the head. If hash differs: RA-2 trigger #3 fires with the (live-hash, manifest-hash) pair as evidence.
4. T18 reads `retention_sweep_runs` at `retention_sweep_runs_snapshot_ts_ms`; for any row in `manifest.per_event_row_counts` whose live count is now lower, T18 attributes the delta to sweep passes recorded between `retention_sweep_runs_snapshot_ts_ms` and now; unattributed deltas fire trigger #3.

None of this requires loading the dump blob in the normal-case (no-tamper) path. The blob is the deep-evidence surface for the post-trigger investigation; the manifest is the routine-detection surface. This is a clean strengthening.

**Verdict:** RA-2 compensating control #4 is STRENGTHENED by T17. No BLOCK from threat-modeler.

#### Architect ask #5 verdict — RA-2 trigger #3 is NOT re-opened

Walking each of the four re-open triggers against T17's design:

1. **Platform-admin compromise.** T17 does not change the `audit_writer_role` reach; the new `backup_writer_role` is a sibling role with its own GRANTs (explicit SELECT on `BACKUP_TABLES` + EXECUTE on the SECURITY DEFINER backup functions; NO `GRANT` on `audit_log` writes beyond `backup_emit_manifest_written` which is itself bounded by the function body's hard-coded event_type). A platform-admin compromise has the same blast radius as before; T17 does not expand it. **Not fired.**
2. **Authenticity challenge.** T17 strengthens the authenticity story (the manifest carries `sha256` over the dump bytes, `kid` over the encryption envelope, `audit_log_head` over the chain state, `schedule_hash` over the retention schedule version, `node_runtime_pin` over the toolchain). An authenticity challenge has MORE evidence to point at, not less. **Not fired.**
3. **Current divergence.** T17 is the witness; T18 is the detector. T17's deployment does not by itself create a divergence — it creates the surface for detecting one. The first divergence detected post-T18 deployment would fire trigger #3, but that is the trigger doing its job, not the trigger being re-opened by architectural change. **Not fired by T17's deployment.**
4. **Expansion of `audit_writer_role` reach.** T17 does not expand `audit_writer_role`. The new `backup_writer_role` is a sibling, not a subset/superset. The new `backup.manifest_written` and `backup.hard_deleted` event types are emitted via the dedicated `backup_emit_manifest_written` SECURITY DEFINER function, NOT via the general `audit_log` insert path. **Not fired.**

**Verdict:** None of the four re-open triggers fires. RA-2 trigger #3 is NOT re-opened by T17. Architect's claim validated.

#### Architect ask #6 verdict — HG-10 NOT firing is defensible

T17 ships zero user-facing copy. The backup pass is a background system pass; the retention pass is a background system pass; the restore pass is operator-driven via a runbook (not user-facing). The `backup.manifest_written` and `backup.hard_deleted` audit rows are written under the synthetic `system:backup-pass` actor pseudonym — they are NOT surfaced to the user via any UI in T17 or T17.1.

PIPEDA Principle 4.8 (Openness) requires that an organisation make its policies and practices relating to the management of personal information readily available. The relevant policies for T17 are:

- **The privacy policy** (T17.1 ratifies — generic "we back up your data on a 42-day rolling window in ca-central-1 under encryption at rest" copy lives there; HG-10 covers privacy-policy changes if they happen).
- **The audit log** itself is the operational openness surface — `backup.manifest_written` rows are visible to a user requesting their data per PIPEDA Principle 4.9 (Individual Access), filtered to rows where the user's pseudonym is in `meta` (none, in this case — backup is a system actor; the user does not appear in the audit row). The user's RIGHT to know that backups happen is honoured at the policy layer; the SPECIFIC backup events are operational telemetry not legally required to be surfaced per-event.
- **No new user interaction surface** is introduced by T17 or T17.1 — no "your data was backed up" notification, no "your data will be hard-deleted in N days" notice, no "restore in progress" indicator. All of these would be new HG-10 surfaces if added; none of them are added.

HG-10 (user-facing pre-deletion copy / sensitive interaction surface) does not apply to a background system pass with no user touchpoint. The existing HG-10-covered surfaces (export consent dialog, recovery flow, panic wipe) are unchanged.

**Verdict:** HG-10 NOT firing is defensible. PIPEDA Principle 4.8 is preserved through the policy + audit-log paths. No BLOCK from threat-modeler.

#### Architect ask #7 verdict — Cross-border egress invariant preserved

The library's `BackupStore.putWithObjectLock` exposes `cross_region_destination_refused` as a structured rejection reason. The library NEVER specifies a region in its calls — the bucket region is a deployment-time concern T17.1 ratifies — but the structured rejection vocabulary explicitly includes this reason so a misconfigured production deploy (e.g., a bucket inadvertently created in `us-east-1`) surfaces the failure visibly rather than silently shipping data abroad.

Verification path:

- **Library side (T17):** `MemoryBackupStore.__debugForceCrossRegionDestinationRefused(true)` flips the next `putWithObjectLock` call to return `{committed: false, reason: 'cross_region_destination_refused'}`. The library's `runBackupPass` handles this as a normal upload failure (F-82 path) — the manifest transitions to `aborted_cross_region_destination_refused`, the pass returns `{status: 'errored', error_code: 'backup_upload_failed', upload_reason: 'cross_region_destination_refused'}`, the `A-BACKUP-001`-or-similar alert symbol is returned (operator notice). No data is uploaded; no silent egress.
- **Production side (T17.1):** `SupabaseBackupStore.putWithObjectLock` checks the bucket's region against an expected `'ca-central-1'` constant (sourced from `BACKUP_BUCKET_REGION = 'ca-central-1'` env-constant); if the bucket region differs, return `cross_region_destination_refused` WITHOUT attempting the put. The runbook (T17.1 deliverable) ratifies the bucket region pin; any departure is a flagged decision per Hard Rule #4 + a re-opening of ADR-0001.

This is a coherent library-side guard rail: the structured rejection is the operator-visible signal; the production check is the enforcement layer; the bucket region pin is the configuration ratification. ADR-0001 invariant preserved.

**Verdict:** Cross-border egress invariant preserved. No BLOCK.

#### Architect ask #8 verdict — No new subprocessor

ADR-0010 ratifies Sentry as the only non-Supabase subprocessor. Walking T17's dependencies:

- **Encryption key:** `committee_data_key` (ADR-0007). Held inside the Supabase Postgres trust boundary. No KMS. No external signer. Re-encrypt-on-rotation explicitly rejected (would defeat object-lock; defeats the at-rest immutability contract).
- **Storage:** Supabase Storage bucket `backups-ca-central-1` (T17.1). In-scope Supabase service; in-scope `ca-central-1` region.
- **Scheduler:** pg_cron (T17.1). Postgres extension; in-scope Supabase.
- **Hash function:** `crypto.createHash('sha256')` (Node native, via OpenSSL). In-scope toolchain; `node_runtime_pin` field traces the binding.
- **No third-party signer.** No DocuSign, no Cloudflare R2, no S3-compatible third party (Wasabi, Backblaze), no external KMS (AWS KMS, GCP KMS, Azure Key Vault, HashiCorp Vault). The S3-compatible object-lock policy is enforced by Supabase Storage's S3-compatible API surface — which is Supabase, not AWS.
- **No external alert sink at the library boundary.** A-BACKUP-001/002/003 alert wiring lands in T17.1 + observability-setup; the alert sinks (Sentry; ADR-0010 ratified) are in-scope.

ADR-0010 single-subprocessor posture preserved. No new dependency snuck in.

**Verdict:** No new subprocessor. No BLOCK.

#### Residual assessment (aggregate)

All sixteen findings score Low at the library boundary (T17). Five carry a T17.1-deferred component that is required before the production wire-up clears: F-71 (bucket-policy ratification), F-74 (lifecycle policy backstop), F-75 (A-BACKUP-001 alert sink), F-79 + F-80 (pgTAP column assertions on `backup_manifests`), F-83 (T18 integrity-job consumer). One — F-75 — is "Low (CI) / Medium (production-untested)" until A-BACKUP-001 is wired by observability-setup after T17.1. No finding is Critical or High at any horizon.

Aggregate posture: **Low residual** for the backup-posture family with the T17.1 deferred items tracked as carry-forwards. F-48 (the pre-existing §3.7 entry on dump-key adjacency) is **closed by F-73** when T17.1 ships — the kid-recording posture under ADR-0007 supersedes the "key in 1Password + paper" narrative because the encryption key is structurally inside the Supabase Postgres trust boundary, not adjacent to the bucket. F-49 (the pre-existing §3.7 entry on bucket-credential ransomware-delete) is **closed by F-71 + F-75** when T17.1 ships — object-lock at the store boundary structurally prevents the overwrite/delete-within-window attack the F-49 narrative warned about.

#### Re-open triggers

This section re-opens if any of the following:

1. A new audit-log event type bound to backup is added without all six mirrors (TS const, SQL function, SQL schedule table, RETENTION_SCHEDULE row, BackupTable closed allowlist if it's a new target table, scripts/check-audit-enum-coverage.sh). The drift test (F-70) catches the BackupTable half in CI; the audit-log enum dance (ADR-0003 Amendment A) catches the rest.
2. `BACKUP_OBJECT_LOCK_DAYS` or `BACKUP_HARD_DELETE_DAYS` is changed without an ADR-0012 amendment + this ADR-0018's mirror update + the SQL bucket-policy update (three mirrors; CI drift test in T17.1 catches the TS-vs-SQL drift; ADR-0012 catches the policy ratification).
3. The `committee_data_key` anchor is replaced by an external KMS or per-backup random key (Option B(ii) or B(iii) from ADR-0018). Re-opens ADR-0007 + ADR-0010 + this entry; F-73 re-scores under a different key hierarchy.
4. The single-tx wrapper in T17.1 (`writeManifestPending` + `putWithObjectLock` + `transitionManifestStatus` in one Postgres tx) is removed in favour of a multi-step posture without tx wrapping. F-72 + F-82 re-score because the rollback contract becomes best-effort instead of structural.
5. The two-layer hard-delete (lifecycle policy + explicit pass) is reduced to one layer. F-74 + F-75 re-score because the defense-in-depth backstop is removed.
6. A second backup destination is added (e.g., off-Supabase to an external Canadian bucket for "ransomware insurance"). Cross-border verification reactivates per Hard Rule #4; ADR-0010 single-subprocessor posture is re-opened; F-73 + F-84 re-score under a new trust boundary.
7. The closed `BACKUP_TABLES` allowlist is opened to caller-supplied table-list (e.g., a "partial-dump for testing" config field is added). F-70 + F-84 re-score; the partial-dump posture would also require a separate manifest schema variant to track which tables were in vs out.
8. Restore-as-superuser is changed to a non-superuser path (e.g., a "restore via Edge Function with RLS-aware logic" model). New surface for restore-side RLS enforcement; B8 boundary changes shape; new finding for "restore-as-non-superuser correctness."
9. T17.1 introduces a backup-completion dependency in the T16 sweep (forbidden by ADR-0018 Decision §13). The CI no-import test catches this; if disabled, ADR-0017 + ADR-0018 both re-open.

#### Handoff to test-writer

Each F-### below maps to exactly one test (or test file) in `apps/web/test/T17/` (library scope) or `supabase/tests/T17_1/` (SQL + bucket scope, deferred). The test-writer's deliverable for T17 is the library-scope set; the T17.1 set lands when that sibling ships.

Snapshot-pin the three field names — rename fails CI. Runtime: `runBackupPass` computes `lock_until_ms` via `nowMs + BACKUP_OBJECT_LOCK_DAYS * MS_PER_DAY` exclusively (intercept via `__debugListPutCalls`). | `apps/web/test/T17/no-caller-supplied-config.test.ts` (+ `apps/web/test/T17/fixtures/poisoned-config.ts`) | T17 (library); SQL signature DEFERRED to T17.1 |
| F-85 | `.test-d.ts` `keyof BackupStore` does NOT include any string starting with `__debug`. `TestBackupStore extends BackupStore` adds them. `apps/web/src/lib/backup/index.ts` re-exports do NOT include `MemoryBackupStore`, `TestBackupStore`, `__debug*`, `__assertBackupTableExhaustive`. | `apps/web/test/T17/test-store-split.test-d.ts` + `apps/web/test/T17/index-surface.test.ts` | T17 (library) |

##### Five cross-cutting properties the suite MUST establish (load-bearing)

(a) **No caller-supplied `object_ref` / `table_list` / `lock_duration_ms` compiles.** Static (TypeScript) assertion lives in F-84; the test suite includes a `tsc --noEmit` invocation against `apps/web/test/T17/fixtures/poisoned-config.ts` that attempts to construct `BackupPassConfig` with each of the three forbidden fields and asserts the compile fails with an `excess property` error. The ESLint rule `no-spread-into-backup-tables` is exercised by a poisoned fixture file (CI-only directory) that is asserted to fail lint.

(b) **Closed-allowlist drift fails CI.** F-70's set-equality + frozen-ness + §PI inventory pinning assertions plus a "scrub-and-restore" fixture that temporarily removes one entry from `BACKUP_TABLES` (via mutation of a deep-cloned copy fed through a test-only injection point) and asserts the drift test fails. Adding a non-existent table name to a deep-cloned copy and asserting the drift test fails. ESLint rule `no-spread-into-backup-tables` fires on a poisoned fixture.

(c) **Manifest 'pending' precedes 'committed' precedes audit-row write order (F-72 variant).** The test asserts the order by reading `__debugListManifests()` and `__debugListAuditRows()` after a clean pass: the manifest's state-transition timestamps go `pending → committed`, and the `backup.manifest_written` audit row's `ts_ms` is strictly greater than the manifest's `committed_at_ms` (which is greater than `started_at_ms`). T17.1's pgTAP suite re-asserts the property at the SQL boundary by wrapping steps 7–9 in a single Postgres tx and asserting the tx commits atomically.

(d) **F-83 head-pointer field is present and structurally typed.** Every committed manifest in a fixture suite of 10 passes carries `audit_log_head: {id, ts_ms, hash}` (or null on empty chain), `per_event_row_counts: Record<string, number>` (or {}), `retention_sweep_runs_snapshot_ts_ms: number` (non-zero). The three field names are snapshot-pinned — a future rename ("let's call it `chain_head`") fails the snapshot test in CI before merge. T18's reconciliation join inherits this contract via G-T17-RA2-ANCHOR-CONSUMER.

(e) **Hard-delete refusal pre-window returns structured `still_locked` rejection.** F-75's harness-forced state (manifest at -45d but lock_until_ms in the future) → `deleteObjectIfUnlocked` returns `{deleted: false, reason: 'still_locked'}` AND `result.would_fire_alert === 'A-BACKUP-001'`. The library returns the alert symbol; the alert sink is wired in T17.1 + observability-setup. This is the structural defense against early-release lifecycle misconfiguration AND adversarial bucket-policy mutation; the test pins the refusal at the library boundary.

##### Handoff envelope

- **To test-writer:** ADR-0018 §12 originally listed F-70..F-85 as placeholders; this §3.10 ratifies the F-### range AS-IS (no renumbering needed — F-70..F-85 are sequential after §3.9's F-55..F-69 and have no collision in this file). ADR-0018's threat-model cross-reference section (Follow-ups bullet 4) is updated below the table to confirm F-70..F-85 are final. All sixteen tests are mandatory for T17's four-way reviewer pass clearance; eight carry `[T17.1 deferred]` tags whose tests land later but whose acceptance criteria are recorded now: F-70 (cross-mirror SQL drift), F-71 (bucket policy), F-72 (single-tx wrapper), F-74 (lifecycle policy backstop), F-75 (A-BACKUP-001 sink), F-76 (SQL `xact_start()` ordering), F-79 + F-80 (pgTAP column assertions), F-83 (T18 integrity-job consumer).
- **To security-reviewer:** at diff time on T17 PR, verify F-70 (drift CI + ESLint), F-71 (object-lock cooperative-caller defense), F-72 (F-24 inversion state machine), F-79 (pseudonym top-level only), F-80 (manifest no pseudonyms), F-81 (no PII in errors), F-82 (no false completion), F-83 (RA-2 anchor preservation — load-bearing — confirm the snapshot-pin test fires on rename), F-84 (no caller-supplied config — confirm `tsc --noEmit` fixture test), F-85 (TestStore type split). At diff time on T17.1 PR (deferred), verify G-T17-1 advisory lock, G-T17-3 SECURITY DEFINER signatures, G-T17-4 cross-mirror drift, G-T17-5 object-lock duration mirror, G-T17-6 enum extension dance, G-T17-BUCKET-POLICY-RATIFY.
- **To privacy-reviewer:** PI inventory for `backup_manifests` (no PI; structural metadata only — `run_id`, `sha256`, kid, counts, head-pointer tuple, snapshot timestamps, schedule_hash, node_runtime_pin; no pseudonyms, no target_ids of PI records) lands in T17.1 per G-T17-7. ADR-0018 §Compliance check confirms PIPEDA Principle 4.5 + 4.7 + 4.8 alignment; HG-10 NOT firing is defensible (architect ask #6 verdict above; PIPEDA Principle 4.8 preserved via privacy-policy + audit-log paths). Cross-border transfers: NONE introduced by this surface (architect ask #7 verdict; library exposes `cross_region_destination_refused` structured rejection; T17.1 ratifies the `ca-central-1` bucket region; ADR-0001 invariant preserved). Subprocessor posture: ADR-0010 preserved (architect ask #8 verdict; no KMS, no external signer, no third-party bucket).
- **To user (human-gate items):**
  - **HG-15 (re-fires at T17.1 PR submission)** for the new physical table `backup_manifests` AND the new Supabase Storage bucket `backups-ca-central-1` with object-lock policy. Recorded in ADR-0018 §Compliance check + sibling task spec #15.
  - **HG-10 explicitly NOT firing** in this pass (architect ask #6 verdict above; ADR-0018 §Compliance check; T17 ships zero user-facing copy).
  - **HG-9 (retention schedule) ratified 2026-05-22** for ADR-0012 amendment; NOT re-firing in this pass.
  - **No new HG fires in T17 itself.**

---

### 3.11 Audit-log integrity (T18 library + T18.1 SQL)

Source: ADR-0019 (T18 audit-log integrity library + MemoryIntegrityStore), 2026-05-23. Closes RA-2 compensating control #3 ("the T18 chain-integrity job runs at least daily and on every key rotation and every export") by making the witness's detection algorithm operationally testable: the two detection surfaces — chain-walk (in-place mutation) and backup-diff (pivot-rewrite) — are both pinned at the library boundary, and the reconciliation rule that distinguishes attributed sweep-driven divergence from unattributed tamper-driven divergence is the structural separator between an A-INTEGRITY-002 false-positive flood and a silently-swallowed tamper. This sub-section scores F-86..F-100 as the authoritative T18 surface. The §3.10 carry-forward `G-T17-RA2-ANCHOR-CONSUMER` is closed library-side here (T18 reads `manifest.audit_log_head`, `manifest.per_event_row_counts`, `manifest.retention_sweep_runs_snapshot_ts_ms` per the snapshot-pinned contract).

**Scope split:** F-86..F-100 are scored as a family. Library-scope assertions land in T18 (CI tests against `MemoryIntegrityStore`). SQL-scope and infrastructure-scope assertions land in T18.1 (pgTAP, `SupabaseIntegrityStore`, `integrity_check_runs` table + migration, optional `audit_chain_anchors` table, pg_cron 04:30 ET daily + Mon 00:00 ET weekly, Edge Function `post_rotation` + `post_export` trigger surface, `pg_advisory_xact_lock` coordination with backup pass, A-AUDIT-001 / A-INTEGRITY-001 / A-INTEGRITY-002 alert wiring, off-app weekly anchor email delivery to worker co-chair). Each row tags `[T18]` or `[T18.1 deferred]` for the test-writer. **HG-10 explicitly does NOT fire** (zero user-facing copy — operator-facing alerts only; verdict below). **HG-15 fires at T18.1 PR submission** (new physical `integrity_check_runs` table + optional `audit_chain_anchors` table; ADR-0019 §Sibling task spec). **HG-9 does NOT re-fire** — the three new audit-log enum values ride the standard ADR-0003 Amendment A extension dance.

#### Trust boundaries this introduces

- **B6.2 — `integrity_check_role` boundary (added here; activates at T18.1; library shape preserved in T18).** A non-login `integrity_check_role` in T18.1 holds `GRANT EXECUTE` on the `SECURITY DEFINER` integrity-check functions (`integrity_check_walk_audit_chain_segment`, `integrity_check_read_latest_backup_manifest`, `integrity_check_list_sweep_runs_through`, `integrity_check_read_chain_rows_by_ids`, `integrity_check_emit_run_and_mismatches`, `integrity_check_emit_chain_anchor_weekly`, `integrity_check_has_open_run_within_window`, `integrity_check_record_run_started`, `integrity_check_extract_chain_head`). It is a SIBLING role to `retention_service_role` (B6, T16.1), `backup_writer_role` (B6.1, T17.1), and `audit_writer_role` — NOT an expansion of any. It has NO `BYPASSRLS`; SELECT-only on `audit_log` + `retention_sweep_runs` + `backup_manifests`; INSERT only via the dedicated `integrity_check_emit_*` SECURITY DEFINER functions whose bodies hard-code the closed event-type allowlist (`audit.integrity_check.ran`, `audit.integrity_check.mismatch`, `audit.chain_anchor.weekly`); no UPDATE; no DELETE (DELETE remains exclusively `retention_service_role` aged-row path). The function bodies hard-code the trigger discriminator (closed allowlist); no caller-supplied predicate / WHERE / pivot / row-range / runtime_pin path. The library half (T18) mirrors this at the type level: `IntegrityStore` forbids caller-supplied `predicate`, `where`, `pivot`, `row_range`, `start_id`, `end_id`, `table_name`, `backup_manifest_id`, `runtime_pin`; the only configurable surface is `dry_run` + `lease_window_ms`. Treat B6.2 as "type-level in T18, role-level in T18.1." Reference: ADR-0019 Decision §3 + §5 + §6 + §11; sibling task spec items #1, #2, #4, #12.
- **Diagram note (consolidated diagram, §1 of this file).** B6.2 sits inside the Supabase-cloud box adjacent to B6 (`retention_service_role`) and B6.1 (`backup_writer_role`) and the existing `audit_writer_role`. Edge flow: pg_cron daily 04:30 ET → `integrity_check_role` SECURITY DEFINER `runIntegrityCheck({trigger:'scheduled'})` wrapper → (1) lease check, (2) record run row in `running` state, (3) read latest committed backup manifest, (4) runtime-pin coherence check, (5) chain walk in 1000-row batches up to 20000 row cap, (6) backup-diff for rows older than `manifest.committed_at_ms - 1h`, (7) reconciliation walker per Option G binding rule, (8) emit each mismatch audit row BEFORE alert fan-out (F-87), (9) emit `audit.integrity_check.ran` summary row LAST in tx (F-88), (10) state machine terminal transition. Separate pg_cron weekly Mon 00:00 ET drives `runWeeklyChainAnchor` → emit `audit.chain_anchor.weekly` row → T18.1 Edge Function reads and sends off-app email to worker co-chair (manual backstop, NOT a control). Edge Function `post_rotation` + `post_export` paths fire `runIntegrityCheck({trigger:'post_rotation'|'post_export'})` within the 5-min upper bound per F-50. When the diagram is next refreshed, add a B6.2 box adjacent to B6 + B6.1; show pg_cron 04:30 ET + Mon 00:00 ET edges; show Edge Function trigger edges from rotation + export pipelines.

#### Data flows (T18 library shape; T18.1 SQL shape mirrors)

```
[Integrity check pass — per ADR-0019 §5 algorithm]
  Caller (CI test in T18; pg_cron 04:30 ET + Edge Functions post_rotation / post_export in T18.1)
    -> runIntegrityCheck({store, config: {trigger}})
       1. store.hasOpenIntegrityRunWithinWindow(nowMs, INTEGRITY_DEFAULT_LEASE_WINDOW_MS = 5min)
            if true -> return {status: 'skipped', reason: 'pass_already_in_window'}
            (F-59 lease pattern; T18.1 SQL half is pg_advisory_xact_lock SHARED with backup
             per Option F; key hashtext('audit_chain_global'); G-T16-1 mirror)
       2. run_id = generateRunId() with 'ic_' prefix (G-T16-PRIV-3 PII-shape rejection)
       3. store.recordIntegrityRunStarted({run_id, trigger, started_at_ms: nowMs})
            // F-72 state machine: status='running' BEFORE any chain walk
            // If throws -> return {status: 'errored', error_code: 'run_start_failed'}
       4. snapshotToken = store.snapshot()             // F-58 rollback hook
       5. manifest = await store.readLatestCommittedBackupManifest()
            // G-T17-RA2-ANCHOR-CONSUMER; snapshot-pinned three-field consumer:
            //   manifest.audit_log_head, manifest.per_event_row_counts,
            //   manifest.retention_sweep_runs_snapshot_ts_ms
            // If null (Phase-0 / no committed manifest): backup-diff SKIPPED; chain-walk proceeds
       6. if manifest !== null:
            livePin = store.readNodeRuntimePin()        // G-T11-23 hash-determinism pin
            if livePin.node_version !== manifest.node_runtime_pin.node_version
               OR livePin.openssl_version !== manifest.node_runtime_pin.openssl_version:
              store.restore(snapshotToken)
              return {status: 'errored', error_code: 'runtime_pin_mismatch'}
              // OPERATIONAL error, NOT A-AUDIT-001 (false-positive prevention; F-93)
       7. // Chain walk (primary detection surface)
          for batch in walkAuditChainSegment({batch_size: 1000, start_after_id: cursor}):
            for row in batch:
              expected_hash = BLAKE2b-256(canonical_json(row + row.prev_hash))
              if expected_hash !== row.hash: push chain_walk mismatch (F-89)
              if row.prev_hash !== BLAKE2b-256(prev_row.hash): push chain_walk mismatch (F-89)
              if row.id !== prev_row.id + 1 AND gap NOT attributable to a sweep:
                push chain_walk gap mismatch (F-90)
              if rows_walked >= 20000: break with status='capped' + resume_after_id (F-99)
       8. // Backup-diff (RA-2 trigger #3 detection surface; only if manifest != null)
          if manifest !== null AND manifest.audit_log_head !== null:
            cutoff_ts_ms = manifest.committed_at_ms - INTEGRITY_BACKUP_DIFF_BUFFER_MS (1h)
            for dump_row in manifest.id_range where dump_row.ts < cutoff_ts_ms:
              live_row = await store.readChainRowsByIds([dump_row.id])
              if live_row present AND (live.hash !== dump.hash OR live.prev_hash !== dump.prev_hash):
                push backup_diff mismatch (F-91; pivot-rewrite detection)
              if live_row absent:
                apply reconciliation (step 9)
              // Rows newer than cutoff are NOT walked (no false-positive on post-dump inserts)
       9. // Reconciliation (Option G binding rule; F-92)
          for absent_row in absent_from_live_but_in_dump:
            sweeps = await store.listRetentionSweepRunsThrough(manifest.retention_sweep_runs_snapshot_ts_ms)
            for sweep in sweeps where sweep.started_at_ms <= absent_row.ts <= sweep.completed_at_ms
                                  AND sweep.per_event_counts[absent_row.event_type] > 0:
              greedy-attribute; decrement sweep's per_event_counts budget
            if no eligible sweep:
              push UNATTRIBUTABLE mismatch (F-92; A-AUDIT-001 AND A-INTEGRITY-002 both fire)
            // per_event_counts[k] missing key treated as 0 (G-T17-9)
            // never reads per_event_counts['__ceiling__'] (G-T16-RECONCILE-CEILING)
      10. // State machine terminal + emission (F-87 + F-88 + F-72)
          await store.emitIntegrityCheckRunAndMismatches({
            run: {...started, terminal_status, completed_at_ms},
            mismatches: mismatch_rows,                  // F-87: each written BEFORE ran row
            ran_row: ran_row                            // F-88: LAST write in tx (omitted if errored)
          })
          // If emit throws -> store.restore(snapshotToken) -> errored / audit_emit_failed
          // (G-T11-29 lesson: no stub success; mismatches re-detected on next pass)
      11. // Build IntegrityRunResult (closed discriminated union)
          return one of:
            { status: 'completed', run_id, ..., would_fire_alert?: 'A-AUDIT-001' |
              readonly ('A-AUDIT-001' | 'A-INTEGRITY-002')[] }
            { status: 'capped', run_id, ..., truncated_to_row_cap: true, resume_after_id }
            { status: 'errored', run_id, error_code: 'run_start_failed' |
              'runtime_pin_mismatch' | 'chain_walk_failed' | 'backup_diff_failed' |
              'audit_emit_failed' }
            { status: 'skipped', reason: 'pass_already_in_window' }
  Errors throughout: {run_id, status, error_code} only (F-100; G-T11-29 / G-T16-PRIV-3 mirror)

[Weekly chain anchor pass — per ADR-0019 §7 algorithm]
  Caller (CI test in T18; pg_cron Mon 00:00 ET in T18.1)
    -> runWeeklyChainAnchor({store})
       1. head = highest-id row from walkAuditChainSegment({start_after_id: null, max_rows: Infinity})
            if empty chain -> return {status: 'skipped', reason: 'empty_chain'}
       2. await store.emitChainAnchorWeekly({event_type: 'audit.chain_anchor.weekly', ...,
            meta: {anchor_at_ms: nowMs, head: {id, ts_ms, hash}}})
       3. return {status: 'completed', anchor_at_ms, head}
  // Off-app email delivery is OUT OF LIBRARY SCOPE; T18.1's Edge Function reads the row
  // and sends to worker co-chair's email-of-record. Manual backstop per RA-2 §4298;
  // absence does NOT re-open RA-2.
```

Classification per surface: `integrity_check_runs` (T18.1) carries NO PI (structural counts + run metadata only — `run_id`, `trigger`, `started_at_ms`, `completed_at_ms`, `status`, `rows_walked`, `mismatches_count`, `attributable_count`, `unattributable_count`, `backup_diff_performed`, `backup_manifest_run_id`, `resume_after_id`, `node_runtime_pin`, `schedule_hash`; mirrors `retention_sweep_runs`). Optional `audit_chain_anchors` (T18.1, implementer choice) carries NO PI (head-pointer triple + delivery timestamp only). The three new audit-log event-type rows: `audit.integrity_check.ran` carries `{run_id, trigger, started_at_ms, completed_at_ms, status, rows_walked, mismatches_count, attributable_count, unattributable_count, backup_diff_performed, backup_manifest_run_id, resume_after_id, node_runtime_pin, schedule_hash}` in `meta` with synthetic `HMAC('system:integrity-check')` actor_pseudonym at top level (mirrors `system:retention` / `system:backup-pass`); `audit.integrity_check.mismatch` carries `{run_id, detected_via, row_id (the audit_log.id of the mismatching row — structurally bigint, non-PII), expected_hash, actual_hash, prev_hash_match, attribution_attempted, backup_manifest_run_id?}` — explicitly NO `actor_pseudonym` of the mismatching row's actor, NO `target_id` of the mismatching row, NO `meta` excerpt of the mismatching row's content (G-T17-PRIV-7); `audit.chain_anchor.weekly` carries `{anchor_at_ms, head: {id, ts_ms, hash}}` only. Residency: ca-central-1 (no new processor; T18.1 reads `audit_log` + `retention_sweep_runs` + `backup_manifests` all in `ca-central-1`). Retention: `integrity_check_runs` rows = 24 months (operational telemetry; mirrors `retention_sweep_runs` recommended class); `audit.integrity_check.ran` audit rows = 24 months; `audit.integrity_check.mismatch` audit rows = 7 years (load-bearing forensic); `audit.chain_anchor.weekly` audit rows = 7 years (load-bearing forensic; off-app email anchor target).

#### STRIDE scoring table — F-86 through F-100

| F-### | Lineage (architect ask) | STRIDE | Asset / code path | Mitigation (testable assertion) | Residual | Test obligation | Scope |
|---|---|---|---|---|---|---|---|
| F-86 | F-55 / F-70 mirror — closed-allowlist drift | T (Tampering of code paths via mirror drift) + E (Elevation via missing/extra allowlist entry expanding the integrity-check event-type surface or dropping a required event) | `IntegrityCheckEventType` union vs `INTEGRITY_CHECK_EVENT_TYPES` frozen const; ADR-0019 Decision §2 | *"Library CI parses `INTEGRITY_CHECK_EVENT_TYPES` + asserts every value in the closed `IntegrityCheckEventType` union has exactly one allowlist entry; every allowlist entry is in the union; allowlist is `Object.isFrozen`. Removing the literal `'audit.integrity_check.mismatch'` from the const fails CI. Adding a fourth string not in the union fails CI. Every entry has a recommended retention class (`{kind:'fixed_months',months:24}` for ran; `{kind:'fixed_years',years:7}` for mismatch and weekly). No caller-supplied event_type reaches `buildIntegrityCheckRanRow` / `buildIntegrityCheckMismatchRow` / `buildChainAnchorWeeklyRow` — the builders hard-code the literal."* | **Low** (with CI test); without the test this would be Medium-High because removing the mismatch literal would silently disable A-AUDIT-001 routing (RA-2 trigger #3 would fire on the next divergence with no audit-row evidence). | T18-DRIFT-1 (set-equality + freeze), T18-DRIFT-2 (retention-class coverage), T18-DRIFT-3 (no caller-supplied event_type reaches emission). | T18 (library CI). Cross-mirror SQL drift (TS const vs SQL `audit_log.event_type` CHECK constraint widening to include the three new strings) deferred to T18.1 per ADR-0019 sibling task spec #13. |
| F-87 | F-24 lineage — audit-before-alert-fanout | R (Repudiation — A-AUDIT-001 fires but no audit-row evidence exists) + I (Information disclosure of an alert with no forensic anchor) | Mismatch row written BEFORE alert symbol surfaces; ADR-0019 Decision §5 step 10 + Option E | *"Every `audit.integrity_check.mismatch` row appears in `__debugListEmittedAuditRows()` BEFORE the `IntegrityRunResult.would_fire_alert` symbol is observable on the returned object. Test: `__debugCorruptHashAtId(50)` on a 100-row fixture; run integrity check; capture the emitted-rows list AND the result; assert at least one mismatch row exists in the emitted-rows list AND `result.would_fire_alert === 'A-AUDIT-001'`. Test: the emission order within the store is `[mismatch_row_1, ..., mismatch_row_N, ran_row]` (asserted via the store's append-order debug view). Test: a forced emit failure ON the ran row (NOT on a mismatch row) results in NO would_fire_alert on the returned errored result — the alert symbol depends on the full emission succeeding (F-88 coherence)."* | **Low** — F-24 invariant preserved as "mismatch rows precede the alert-symbol return value, which is the library's stand-in for the T18.1 alert fan-out." | T18-AUDIT-BEFORE-ALERT-1 (mismatch row visible before alert symbol), T18-AUDIT-BEFORE-ALERT-2 (emission order pinning). | T18 (library). T18.1 (SECURITY DEFINER wrapper around `runIntegrityCheck` invokes the A-AUDIT-001 sink AFTER the SQL tx commits — the in-tx mismatch rows are durable before the sink fires; pgTAP asserts). |
| F-88 | F-58 lineage — summary LAST in tx | T (Tampering — partial-detection state surfaces if the ran row commits without its mismatch rows) + R (Repudiation — "the integrity check completed" claim is verifiable only when the full atomicity unit lands) | `audit.integrity_check.ran` summary row written LAST in the same transaction as mismatches + run-row terminal transition; ADR-0019 Decision §5 step 10 + Option E + Option H | *"In a clean pass with 3 forced mismatches (`__debugCorruptHashAtId` x3), the order of writes in `__debugListEmittedAuditRows()` is exactly `[mismatch_1, mismatch_2, mismatch_3, ran]`. The `ran` row is the LAST audit row written in the integrity-check transaction. Test: force the emit to throw ON the ran row (`__debugForceEmitException('ran')`); assert NO audit rows are visible afterward (full rollback — the 3 mismatch rows that were queued for emission also do not surface); the run row's terminal status is NOT 'completed' (state machine reverted via `store.restore(snapshotToken)`); the IntegrityRunResult is `{status: 'errored', error_code: 'audit_emit_failed'}`; NO `would_fire_alert` symbol on the errored result. Test: on errored runs, the `audit.integrity_check.ran` row is NEVER emitted (absence is the signal that a pass was attempted but did not complete; mirrors T16 retention.deleted absence semantic)."* | **Low** — F-58 invariant preserved exactly: no integrity-check verdict without its audit row, no audit row without its underlying check. See "Architect ask #3 verdict" + "Architect ask #4 verdict" notes below. | T18-SUMMARY-LAST-1 (write order pinning), T18-SUMMARY-LAST-2 (full rollback on ran-row emit failure), T18-SUMMARY-LAST-3 (no ran row on errored). | T18 (library; `MemoryIntegrityStore` models the tx semantic). T18.1 (`SupabaseIntegrityStore.emitIntegrityCheckRunAndMismatches` wraps INSERT mismatches + UPDATE run-row terminal + INSERT ran-row in a single Postgres tx; pgTAP asserts atomicity). |
| F-89 | NEW SURFACE — primary detection surface | T (Tampering — A5 in-place chain mutation undetected) + R (Repudiation — "the chain is intact" claim has no operational test) | Chain-walk recompute against stored hash + prev_hash linkage; ADR-0019 Decision §5 step 7; observability/audit-log.md §2 chain schema | *"With 100 fixture rows of varied event_types and `__debugCorruptHashAtId(50)` (in-place hash mutation simulating A5 tamper), `runIntegrityCheck({trigger:'scheduled'})` returns `status:'completed'`, `mismatches_count:1`, `would_fire_alert:'A-AUDIT-001'`. The emitted mismatch row carries `meta.detected_via === 'chain_walk'`, `meta.row_id === '50'` (the corrupted row), `meta.prev_hash_match === true` (single-row hash mutation does not break the prev_hash chain — only the hash recompute catches it), `meta.attribution_attempted === false` (chain-walk does not attempt reconciliation). Test: corrupt at row 1 (genesis), at row 50 (middle), at row 100 (head) — three positions all detected with `detected_via:'chain_walk'`. Test: a clean fixture (no corruption) produces `mismatches_count:0` and NO `would_fire_alert` symbol on the result. Test: corrupt `prev_hash` of row 51 (instead of hash of row 50) — also detected, with `meta.prev_hash_match === false`."* | **Low** — primary detection surface is structurally pinned; without it RA-2 has no chain-walk evidence and trigger #3 cannot be cited. | T18-CHAIN-WALK-1 (corrupt-at-50 detected), T18-CHAIN-WALK-2 (genesis + head + middle positions), T18-CHAIN-WALK-3 (prev_hash mismatch distinct from hash mismatch). | T18 (library). T18.1 (SECURITY DEFINER `integrity_check_walk_audit_chain_segment` reads `audit_log` in id-order with `statement_timeout 60s + lock_timeout 5s`; pgTAP asserts equivalence to the library's recompute). |
| F-90 | Coupled with F-89 — sequential-id gap detection with sweep attribution | T (Tampering — chain row deletion masked as a "sweep") + R (Repudiation — "a row went missing" attribution dispute) | Sequential-id gap detection + sweep_run cross-check; ADR-0019 Decision §5 step 7 sub-bullet 3 | *"With 5 fixture rows and `__debugDeleteRowAtId(3)` (no sweep_run accounting for it), integrity check reports a chain-walk mismatch on row 4 — row 4's `prev_hash` no longer matches row 2's `hash` (gap detected via the prev_hash linkage; the gap detection is the prev_hash mismatch). With a sweep_runs fixture seeded via `__debugInsertSweepRunFixture` whose `per_event_counts[row3.event_type] >= 1` AND `started_at_ms <= row3.ts <= completed_at_ms`, the gap is permissively attributed and NO mismatch is reported. Test: both directions pinned (attributed gap → no mismatch; unattributed gap → chain_walk mismatch on the row after the gap). Test: a multi-row gap (delete rows 3 AND 4) requires sweep attribution for BOTH events to suppress the mismatch on row 5; partial attribution surfaces the un-attributed deletion as a mismatch."* | **Low** — gap detection is the chain-walk-side mirror of the backup-diff reconciliation; both directions pinned via the test ensures sweeps are not misclassified as tampers. | T18-GAP-DETECT-1 (unattributed gap surfaces), T18-GAP-DETECT-2 (attributed gap suppressed), T18-GAP-DETECT-3 (partial attribution surfaces residual). | T18 (library; chain-walk uses `MemoryIntegrityStore.listRetentionSweepRunsThrough`). T18.1 (SECURITY DEFINER reads `retention_sweep_runs` in-region; pgTAP asserts). |
| F-91 | RA-2 trigger #3 anchor — **LOAD-BEARING** | T (Tampering — A5 pivot-rewrite attack: re-hash chain forward from a pivot point so chain-walk passes but the dump has the old hashes) + R (Repudiation — "the chain has always been this way" claim defeats chain-walk-alone witnesses) | Backup-diff detection surface; ADR-0019 Decision §5 step 8 + ADR-0018 manifest schema; RA-2 follow-up §4297 | *"**Pivot-rewrite walk-through:** chain-walk alone CANNOT detect a pivot-rewrite — a chain that has been re-hashed forward from row K to the head is internally consistent (every prev_hash matches every preceding hash; every hash matches the canonical-JSON recompute of its row). The chain-walk says 'pass.' Only the backup-diff detects this attack, because the dump captured at `latest_dump_ts` contains row K's PRE-rewrite hash, which differs from the live chain's POST-rewrite hash at the same id. Test: seed 50 rows + insert a backup manifest fixture (`__debugInsertBackupManifestFixture`) whose `audit_log_head.hash` matches the seeded row 50; advance clock 1 hour so all 50 rows are eligible (live rows older than `manifest.committed_at_ms - 1h`); `__debugCorruptHashAtId(10)` (a row older than the 1h dump-buffer cutoff); `runIntegrityCheck({trigger:'scheduled'})`. Assertions: mismatch row's `meta.detected_via === 'backup_diff'`, `meta.row_id === '10'`, `meta.expected_hash === <row 10's dump hash>` (from the manifest fixture), `meta.actual_hash === <corrupted hash>`, `meta.backup_manifest_run_id === <fixture.run_id>`, `meta.prev_hash_match` reflects whether prev_hash also differs; `result.would_fire_alert === 'A-AUDIT-001'`. **CRITICAL inversion:** a row inserted AFTER `manifest.committed_at_ms - 1h` is STRUCTURALLY EXCLUDED from the diff — assert that corrupting a fresh post-dump row does NOT fire backup_diff (only chain_walk would catch it if applicable; no false-positive on legitimate new rows). **If this test breaks, RA-2 trigger #3 fires by construction (re-opening RA-2).**"* | **LOW residual at the library boundary, LOAD-BEARING for RA-2 trigger #3**. The score is conditional on the test fixture remaining executable — see "Architect ask #1 verdict" note below. If F-91 fails (the backup-diff path silently degrades or short-circuits when the manifest is present), RA-2 trigger #3 fires on the next reconciliation pass because the only operational pivot-rewrite detection surface is gone. | T18-BACKUP-DIFF-1 (pivot-rewrite detected with full meta), T18-BACKUP-DIFF-2 (no false-positive on post-dump rows — fresh-row inversion test), T18-BACKUP-DIFF-3 (null manifest → backup-diff skipped, chain-walk proceeds). | T18 (library). T18.1 (`SupabaseIntegrityStore.readChainRowsByIds` reads live `audit_log` rows; the dump bytes are referenced via `manifest.sha256` + object-locked bucket fetch on deep investigation only; routine detection is manifest-vs-live-row hash compare; pgTAP). |
| F-92 | G-T16-8 anchor — Option G binding rule | T (Tampering — chain row deletion masked as legitimate sweep) + R (Repudiation — "we cannot tell sweep from tamper" attribution dispute) + I (Information disclosure — false-positive A-INTEGRITY-002 floods operator into alert fatigue) | Reconciliation walker per ADR-0019 Decision §5 step 9 + Option G; G-T16-8 carry-forward closed library-side; G-T17-9 zero-event-count convention | *"**Both directions pinned (load-bearing).** Direction 1 — attributed (legitimate sweep): seed 50 rows + insert a backup manifest fixture whose `audit_log_head` includes id 30 (event_type `concern.created`). Insert a sweep_run fixture via `__debugInsertSweepRunFixture` with `per_event_counts: {'concern.created': 1}`, `started_at_ms <= row30.ts <= completed_at_ms`, `started_at_ms <= manifest.retention_sweep_runs_snapshot_ts_ms`. `__debugDeleteRowAtId(30)`. `runIntegrityCheck`: assert NO `would_fire_alert` symbol; mismatch row absent from `__debugListEmittedAuditRows()`; `result.attributable_count === 1`; `result.unattributable_count === 0`; `meta.status === 'completed'` on the ran row. Direction 2 — unattributable (tamper): same setup BUT NO eligible sweep_run (`per_event_counts: {'inspection.submitted': 1}` — wrong event_type) OR `started_at_ms > row30.ts` (wrong window). `runIntegrityCheck`: `result.would_fire_alert` contains BOTH `'A-AUDIT-001'` AND `'A-INTEGRITY-002'` (distinct symbols); `result.unattributable_count === 1`; mismatch row present with `meta.attribution_attempted === true`, `meta.actual_hash === null` (live row absent), `meta.detected_via === 'backup_diff'`. Direction 3 — zero-event-count convention: a sweep_run whose `per_event_counts` is missing the key entirely (NOT zero-valued; literally absent) is treated as count=0; the absent row is unattributable. Direction 4 — greedy attribution budget: a sweep with `per_event_counts: {'concern.created': 1}` can attribute exactly 1 row of that event_type; if 2 rows are absent of the same event_type, the second is unattributable. Direction 5 — `__ceiling__` rejection: a sweep_run whose `per_event_counts` contains `__ceiling__` key is REJECTED — the library NEVER reads this key (G-T16-RECONCILE-CEILING; the structural absence is verified by a runtime grep on every read)."* | **LOW residual at the library boundary, LOAD-BEARING correctness property**. The reconciliation rule is the structural separator between the false-positive flood case (A-INTEGRITY-002 fires on every legitimate sweep) and the silent-tamper case (sweep deletes hide tampers). Both directions must be pinned; a one-direction-only test would allow the inverse failure mode through. See "Architect ask #2 verdict" note below. | T18-RECONCILE-1 (attributed direction → no alert), T18-RECONCILE-2 (unattributable direction → both alerts distinct), T18-RECONCILE-3 (zero-event-count convention — missing key = 0), T18-RECONCILE-4 (greedy attribution budget exhaustion), T18-RECONCILE-5 (`__ceiling__` never read). | T18 (library). T18.1 (SECURITY DEFINER `integrity_check_list_sweep_runs_through` returns the snapshot subset; pgTAP asserts the SQL surface matches the library's reconciliation outcome on a parametric fixture set). |
| F-93 | G-T11-23 lineage — hash-determinism pin; OPERATIONAL not A-AUDIT-001 | T (Tampering false-positive — a legitimate Node/OpenSSL upgrade silently changes hash output and chain-walk fires spurious A-AUDIT-001) + D (Denial of service — alert fatigue from spurious post-upgrade fires) | Runtime-pin coherence check before reconciliation; ADR-0019 Decision §5 step 6 + Decision drivers (G-T11-23) | *"Seed a backup manifest with `node_runtime_pin: {node_version: '21.5.0', openssl_version: '3.0.10'}`. `__debugForceRuntimePinMismatch(true)` swaps the live store's `readNodeRuntimePin()` to return a sentinel value that does NOT match the manifest's pin. `runIntegrityCheck({trigger:'scheduled'})` returns `{status:'errored', run_id, error_code:'runtime_pin_mismatch'}`. **Critical assertions:** (a) NO `audit.integrity_check.mismatch` rows are emitted (the error is OPERATIONAL, not adversarial — a toolchain upgrade is not a tamper); (b) NO `would_fire_alert: 'A-AUDIT-001'` on the errored result (false-positive prevention — the chain-walk did NOT execute under a different runtime); (c) the chain-walk pass is SKIPPED (the snapshot is restored via `store.restore(snapshotToken)`; no partial walk state surfaces); (d) the structural error_code is the closed literal `'runtime_pin_mismatch'` — distinct from `'chain_walk_failed'`. T18.1's observability sink routes `runtime_pin_mismatch` to A-INTEGRITY-001-variant (operational), NOT to A-AUDIT-001. Test: a CLEAN runtime pin (live === manifest) proceeds normally and `runtime_pin_mismatch` never fires. Test: an empty manifest (null) SKIPS the runtime-pin check entirely (no manifest = no pin to compare against; chain-walk proceeds independently)."* | **Low** — false-positive prevention is the load-bearing concern; without F-93 every Node 21 → 22 upgrade fires spurious A-AUDIT-001 across all production passes (alert fatigue → real fires missed). See "Architect ask #5 verdict" note below. | T18-RUNTIME-PIN-1 (mismatch → errored + no mismatch rows + no A-AUDIT-001), T18-RUNTIME-PIN-2 (clean pin → proceeds), T18-RUNTIME-PIN-3 (null manifest → skipped check). | T18 (library). T18.1 (`SupabaseIntegrityStore.readNodeRuntimePin` reads `process.versions` from inside the SECURITY DEFINER function context; the SQL wrapper enforces the same coherence check before invoking the chain walk). |
| F-94 | G-T17-PRIV-7 + G-T16-PRIV-1 mirror | I (Information disclosure — mismatch / ran / anchor row leaks PI via meta excerpt of the mismatching row, OR a pseudonym duplicated into meta surfaces via the integrity-job join) | No PII in emitted rows; ADR-0019 Decision §8 + §9 + §10 (mismatch / ran / anchor row meta layouts; verbatim quotable) | *"Structural type test (`.test-d.ts`): `keyof MismatchRowMeta` contains exactly `{run_id, detected_via, row_id, expected_hash, actual_hash, prev_hash_match, attribution_attempted, backup_manifest_run_id?}` — NO `actor_pseudonym`, NO `target_id`, NO `event_type` of the mismatching row, NO `meta` excerpt of the mismatching row, NO `severity` of the mismatching row. Same for `RanRowMeta` and `ChainAnchorWeeklyMeta` against their respective Decision §9 / §10 layouts. Runtime test: emit a `mismatch` row + a `ran` row + a `weekly_anchor` row; deep-grep each `meta` object for: (a) 32-hex strings (would indicate a pseudonym leak — `actor_pseudonym` is the HMAC shape); (b) phone shape `\d{3}-\d{3}-\d{4}`; (c) email shape; (d) UUID shapes other than `run_id` (which uses `ic_` prefix to break 32-hex word boundary per G-T16-PRIV-3 rejection-sample) and `backup_manifest_run_id` (which uses the backup pass's `bp_` prefix per ADR-0018); (e) hex longer than 64 chars except `expected_hash` / `actual_hash` / `head.hash` (which are 64-hex BLAKE2b-256 by construction). Assert zero matches. Test: `actor_pseudonym` appears at the TOP LEVEL of each audit row ONLY — `'actor_pseudonym' in row.meta === false` for all three event types. Test: even `__debugForceMismatch` fixtures CANNOT inject PI shapes into meta — the library's `buildIntegrityCheckMismatchRow` builder strips unknown keys defensively."* | **Low** — privacy invariant pinned at both the type level and the runtime grep level. | T18-NO-PII-MISMATCH-1 (type test on MismatchRowMeta), T18-NO-PII-RAN-1 (type test on RanRowMeta), T18-NO-PII-ANCHOR-1 (type test on ChainAnchorWeeklyMeta), T18-NO-PII-RUNTIME-1 (deep-grep on emitted rows), T18-NO-PII-TOP-LEVEL-1 (actor_pseudonym top-level only). | T18 (library). T18.1 (pgTAP: JSONB structure assertions on `audit_log.meta` for the three new event types; column-existence assertions on `integrity_check_runs`). |
| F-95 | NEW SURFACE — A-AUDIT-001 vs A-INTEGRITY-002 distinct causes | R (Repudiation — alerts conflated; responder cannot distinguish hash mismatch from reconciliation failure) + I (Information disclosure — wrong alert routing surfaces the wrong forensic surface to the wrong responder) | Distinct alert symbols on result; ADR-0019 Option E + Decision §5 step 11 (closed discriminated-union return shape) | *"Three test scenarios assert the `would_fire_alert` shape exactly: Scenario A — chain-walk mismatch ONLY (`__debugCorruptHashAtId(50)`, no manifest fixture or null-manifest path): `result.would_fire_alert === 'A-AUDIT-001'` (single symbol, NOT an array). Scenario B — unattributable backup-diff divergence (F-92 direction 2 setup): `result.would_fire_alert` is a readonly array containing BOTH `'A-AUDIT-001'` AND `'A-INTEGRITY-002'` (distinct symbols; order pinned by library convention but the test asserts set-equality); the mismatch row's `meta.attribution_attempted === true` (signals the reconciliation walker ran). Scenario C — attributable backup-diff divergence (F-92 direction 1 setup): `result.would_fire_alert` is undefined / absent (NEITHER symbol fires); no mismatch row emitted. **Architect-pinned rule:** A-AUDIT-001 fires on the FACT of mismatch (hash-mismatch FOUND, regardless of cause classification); A-INTEGRITY-002 fires on the CAUSE classification failing (reconciliation walker found no eligible sweep_run). The two alerts MAY fire together (Scenario B); they MAY fire independently (Scenario A — A-AUDIT-001 alone on chain-walk-detected); they MUST NOT be conflated."* | **Low** — distinct-causes pinning is the load-bearing operator-facing property (responder uses A-INTEGRITY-002's presence to decide sweep-bug vs adversarial-tamper investigation path). See "Architect ask #6 verdict" note below. | T18-ALERT-DISTINCT-1 (chain-walk → A-AUDIT-001 only), T18-ALERT-DISTINCT-2 (unattributable → both), T18-ALERT-DISTINCT-3 (attributable → neither). | T18 (library symbols). T18.1 + observability-setup (alert sinks: A-AUDIT-001 to operator; A-INTEGRITY-002 to operator with reconciliation-failure context; A-INTEGRITY-001 (missed-cron) wired by observability-setup). |
| F-96 | NEW SURFACE — weekly chain anchor emission (RA-2 manual backstop) | R (Repudiation — no off-app witness to point to in a chain-wide tamper dispute) + I (Information disclosure — operator-facing weekly anchor as the manual backstop surface) | Weekly anchor emission contract; ADR-0019 Decision §7 + Option C; RA-2 §4298 manual backstop | *"`runWeeklyChainAnchor({store})` with seeded 50 rows: emits exactly one `audit.chain_anchor.weekly` row; `meta.head.{id, ts_ms, hash}` matches the highest-id row's `(id, ts_ms, hash)` exactly; `result === {status:'completed', anchor_at_ms, head}`. Absence of the email does NOT fire any alert (manual backstop per RA-2 §4298; absence does NOT re-open RA-2)."* | **Low** — manual backstop, not a compensating control; the row is the in-chain witness, the email is operator-mediated off-app delivery (no subprocessor). | T18-WEEKLY-ANCHOR-1 (head triple match), T18-WEEKLY-ANCHOR-2 (empty chain skipped), T18-WEEKLY-ANCHOR-3 (errored paths emit no row), T18-WEEKLY-ANCHOR-4 (meta.head field-name snapshot pin). | T18 (library; emission only). T18.1 (Edge Function reads the row + sends email to worker co-chair's email-of-record; sibling task spec item #9). |
| F-97 | F-19 / F-84 mirror — no caller-supplied predicate / pivot / WHERE / row-range / runtime_pin | E (Elevation — cooperative caller injects a predicate / pivot / WHERE / row-range to scope the integrity check to a narrow window OR overrides runtime_pin to skip the coherence check OR selects a non-latest backup manifest to compare against a stale snapshot) | `IntegrityCheckRunConfig` type-level closed surface; ADR-0019 Decision §6 + §11; F-19 + ADR-0018 F-84 lineage | *"TypeScript structural assertion (`.test-d.ts`): `IntegrityCheckRunConfig` has NO field whose name matches `/predicate|where|pivot|row_range|start_id|end_id|table_name|backup_manifest_id|runtime_pin|max_rows|batch_size/i`. Runtime test: `runIntegrityCheck` ignores any extra `(config as any).<forbidden_field>` injection (defensive — the library reads only the typed fields). Test: the closed `trigger` union is exhaustive-switched in `runIntegrityCheck` with a `never` cast on the default branch (mirrors F-19 family). Test: the library NEVER calls `store.readLatestCommittedBackupManifest` with a parameter — the production store always returns the latest committed manifest; there is no library code path through which a non-latest manifest can be selected."* | **Low** — F-19 generalized to the integrity surface; cooperative-caller defense is structural at the type level + runtime defensive. | T18-NO-CALLER-CONFIG-1 (type-fail on each forbidden field), T18-NO-CALLER-CONFIG-2 (runtime ignores injected extras), T18-NO-CALLER-CONFIG-3 (exhaustive-switch + never cast on trigger). | T18 (library type-level + runtime). T18.1 (SECURITY DEFINER function signatures hard-code the closed allowlist; pgTAP asserts CHECK constraint on `trigger` column). |
| F-98 | F-65 / F-85 mirror — TestStore split | E (Elevation — production code reaches test-only `__debug*` fixtures and weakens the cooperative-caller defense; e.g., production code forces a runtime_pin mismatch or injects a corrupted hash) | `IntegrityStore` vs `TestIntegrityStore` type-level split + barrel re-export check; ADR-0019 Decision §3 + Option I + Option J | *"Type-level (`.test-d.ts`): `keyof IntegrityStore` does NOT include any string starting with `__debug`. `TestIntegrityStore extends IntegrityStore` and adds `__debugForceMismatch`, `__debugSetClock`, `__debugListRuns`, `__debugListMismatches`, `__debugListEmittedAuditRows`, `__debugInsertFixtureRow`, `__debugCorruptHashAtId`, `__debugDeleteRowAtId`, `__debugInsertBackupManifestFixture`, `__debugInsertSweepRunFixture`, `__debugForceRuntimePinMismatch`, `__debugForceChainWalkException`, `__debugForceEmitException`. | F-99 | F-60 mirror — row-cap + `capped` state | D (Denial of service — pathological canonical-JSON row causes excessive allocation; future scale event >5M rows) + T (Tampering — a hostile actor inserts a series of synthetic rows hoping to time-out the integrity check pass and surface a missed-cron signal) | Library-controlled row cap + state machine `capped` terminal + `resume_after_id`; ADR-0019 Option D + Decision §5 step 7 sub-bullet 4 | *"With 20001 seeded fixture rows and zero mismatches, `runIntegrityCheck({trigger:'scheduled'})` returns `status:'capped'`, `rows_walked:20000`, `mismatches_count:0`, `truncated_to_row_cap:true`, `resume_after_id:<id of row 20000 as string>`. T18.1 (`SupabaseIntegrityStore` cursor management; `statement_timeout 60s + lock_timeout 5s` operational-safety belt; pgTAP asserts). |
| F-100 | F-67 / F-81 mirror — closed-literal error_codes; no PII in errors | I (Information disclosure via error path leak of row content, row_id under a PII-bearing row's actor, event_type of a leaked row, or PI shape in the error message) | Structured-error-not-PII per ADR-0019 Decision §5 step 11 + Decision drivers (G-T11-29 / G-T16-PRIV-3 / G-T17 F-81); closed literal `error_code` union | *"Force each of the four library error_codes: (a) `run_start_failed` via `__debugForceEmitException` on the started run row; (b) `runtime_pin_mismatch` via `__debugForceRuntimePinMismatch(true)`; (c) `chain_walk_failed` via `__debugForceChainWalkException(true)`; (d) `audit_emit_failed` via `__debugForceEmitException` on the terminal emit.
